***rouw.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:rouw.html>rouw</a> (9342)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:rouwen.html>rouwe</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruwe.html>ruwe</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*reuwa</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*hrewwōn</i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*hrewwō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pain, sadness, regret, repentance</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">hrēow</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">rue</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Reue</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Norse" class="extiw" title="w:Old Norse">Old <a href = vnd.unilang:norse.html>Norse</a></a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="non">hryggr</i>. More at <span class="Latn" lang="en">rue</span>. The noun <i><a href = vnd.unilang:rouw.html>rouw</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:belongs.html>belongs</a> to the verb <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rouwen.html>rouwen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p>

</p>
<ol><li>mourning</li>
<li>sorrow, grief</li></ol>

***roven.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:roven.html>roven</a> (16633)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">rôven</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*rōvon</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro">*raubōn</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*raubōną</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roven.html>roven</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to rob</li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>See the etymology of the main entry.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roven.html>roven</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="use-with-mention">Plural form of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">roof</i></span></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Werkwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:werkwoord.html>Werkwoord</a></i></span></h4>
<p><b><a href = vnd.unilang:roven.html>roven</a></b>
</p>
<ol><li><span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic"><a href = vnd.unilang:overgankelijk.html>overgankelijk</a></span> <a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zaken.html>zaken</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:met.html>met</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:geweld.html>geweld</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:toe-eigenen.html>toe-eigenen</a></li></ol>

***royeren.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:royeren.html>royeren</a> (67698)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">roier</i>. <span class="maintenance-line"><i>This etymology <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> incomplete. You can help Wiktionary by elaborating on the origins of this term.</i></span>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:royeren.html>royeren</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>to dismiss, discharge, expel, fire, sack</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Werkwoord"><i><a href = vnd.unilang:werkwoord.html>Werkwoord</a></i></span></h4>

<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm">rosmarin</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">rosmarin</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">rōs marīnus</i>. Secondarily influenced by <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roos.html>roos</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:rose.html>rose</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, for which compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:rosemary.html>rosemary</a></i>.

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">rosencrans</i>. Equivalent to <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:roos.html>roos</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:rose.html>rose</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:krans.html>krans</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">wreath</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rozenkrans.html>rozenkrans</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rozenkransen.html>rozenkransen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rozenkrans.html>rozenkransje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">literally</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <span class="Latn" lang="en">wreath</span> of <span class="Latn" lang="en">roses</span></li>
<li>The <span class="Latn" lang="en">rosary</span>, a Catholic <span class="Latn" lang="en">prayer</span> sequence, consisting of repetitions of <span class="Latn" lang="en">Our Lady</span> and <span class="Latn" lang="en">Our Father</span></li>
<li>A <span class="Latn" lang="en">rosary</span>, Catholic or, less commonly, Anglican <span class="Latn" lang="en">prayer beads</span> used to keep track of the above</li>
<li>An object resembling the wreath:
<ol><li>a deer's <span class="Latn" lang="en">antlers</span>' <span class="Latn" lang="en">knobby</span> edges</li>
<li>the plant <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gnaphalium_dioicum" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gnaphalium dioicum"><i>Gnaphalium dioicum</i></a></span>, now <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Antennaria_dioica" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Antennaria dioica"><i>Antennaria dioica</i></a></span></li></ol></li>
<li>A symbolical meaning of the wreath:
<ol><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">youth</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">virginity</span></li></ol></li></ol>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">rubrike</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">red pigment</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">rubrique</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">rubrīca</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">red ochre</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, the substance used to make red <a href = vnd.unilang:letters.html>letters</a>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruber.html>ruber</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">red</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₁rewdʰ-</i>.

***ruff.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> (59364)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Clipping of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">ruffle</i></span></span>, or possibly from <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">rough</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A circular frill or ruffle on a garment, <i>especially</i> a starched, fluted frill at the neck in Elizabethan and Jacobean England (1560s–1620s).
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><i><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr></i> <b>1596–1599</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare" class="extiw" title="w:William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>,  “<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_IV,_Part_2" class="extiw" title="w:Henry IV, Part 2">The Second Part of <a href = vnd.unilang:henry.html>Henry</a> the Fourth, containing His Death: And the Coronation of King <a href = vnd.unilang:henry.html>Henry</a> the Fift</a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Folio" class="extiw" title="w:First Folio"><a href = vnd.unilang:mr.html>Mr</a>. William Shakespeares Comedies, <a href = vnd.unilang:histories.html>Histories</a>, amp; <a href = vnd.unilang:tragedies.html>Tragedies</a>: Published <a href = vnd.unilang:according.html>According</a> to the True Originall <a href = vnd.unilang:copies.html>Copies</a></a></cite>, London |  Printed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">Isaac Iaggard</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Ed[ward] Blount</a>, published 1623, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/606515358">606515358</a></small>, Act II, scene iv, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=uNtBAQAAMAAJamp;pg=RA1-PA49">page 83, column 1</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">You a Captaine? you ſlaue, for what? for tearing a poore <a href = vnd.unilang:whores.html>Whores</a> <b>Ruffe</b> in a Bawdy-houſe? <a href = vnd.unilang:hee.html>Hee</a> a Captaine? hang him Rogue, <a href = vnd.unilang:hee.html>hee</a> liues vpon mouldie ſtew'D-Pruines, and dry'<a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:cakes.html>Cakes</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1960</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P._G._Wodehouse" class="extiw" title="w:P. G. Wodehouse">P[elham] G[renville] Wodehouse</a>,  chapter XII, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeeves_in_the_Offing" class="extiw" title="w:Jeeves in the Offing">Jeeves in the Offing</a></cite>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barrie_%26_Jenkins" class="extiw" title="w:Barrie amp; Jenkins">Herbert Jenkins</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/1227855">1227855</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">"When <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> first forgathered, I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> sitting on the floor with a chair round my neck." "Like an Elizabethan <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>, as worn by Thomas Botway." "Otway," I <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a> stiffly.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Anything formed with plaits or flutings like a frill.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1742</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Pope" class="extiw" title="w:Alexander Pope">[Alexander] Pope</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dunciad" class="extiw" title="w:The Dunciad">The New Dunciad: <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span> With the Illustrations of Scriblerus, and Notes Variorum</a></cite>, 2nd edition, London |  Printed for J. H. Hubbard, in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Bailey" class="extiw" title="w:Old Bailey">Old-Bailey</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/837260495">837260495</a></small>, lines 395–398, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gHRbAAAAQAAJamp;pg=PA25">pages 24–25</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Fair from its humble <a href = vnd.unilang:bed.html>bed</a> I rear'd this flow'<a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>r</a>; / Suckled, and chear'd, with air, and ſun, and ſhow'<a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>r</a>; / Soft on the paper <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> its leaves I ſpread, / Bright with the gilded button <a href = vnd.unilang:tipt.html>tipt</a> its head; <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="use-with-mention">Senses relating to animals.</span>
<ol><li><i>Philomachus pugnax</i> (syn. <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Calidris_pugnax" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Calidris pugnax"><i>Calidris pugnax</i></a></span>), a gregarious, medium-sized wading bird of Eurasia; <i>specifically</i>, a male of the species which develops a distinctive <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> and ear tufts during mating season (the female <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> called a <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">reeve</i>).
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1986</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desmond_Nethersole-Thompson" class="extiw" title="w:Desmond Nethersole-Thompson"><a href = vnd.unilang:desmond.html>Desmond</a> Nethersole-Thompson</a> |  Maimie Nethersole-Thompson,  “New or Returning Waders”, in  <cite>Waders: Their Breeding, Haunts and <a href = vnd.unilang:watchers.html>Watchers</a></cite>, Calton, Staffordshire |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T._%26_A._D._Poyser" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:T. amp; A. D. Poyser"><a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>. amp; A. D. Poyser</a>, <small>→ISBN</small> |  republished as  <cite>Waders: Their Breeding, Haunts and <a href = vnd.unilang:watchers.html>Watchers</a></cite> (Poyser Monographs), London |  <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>. amp; A. D. Poyser, 2010, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ivvUBAAAQBAJamp;pg=PA323">page 323</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">A reeve <a href = vnd.unilang:shows.html>shows</a> her readiness to copulate by <a href = vnd.unilang:crouching.html>crouching</a> in a particular residence. In a crowded <a href = vnd.unilang:lek.html>lek</a> she selects an individual <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> by turning towards him while still <a href = vnd.unilang:crouching.html>crouching</a>. Some <b>ruffs</b> are thus chosen frequently while others are never selected. <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a></b> and reeve only copulate after she <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> crouched and <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> sometimes nibbled the <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> at the back of the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>’s head.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1991</b>,  <a href = vnd.unilang:johan.html>Johan</a> G. <a href = vnd.unilang:van.html>van</a> Rhijn,  “The Vigilant Mother”, in  <cite>The <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a>: Individuality in a Gregarious Wading Bird</cite>, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T._%26_A._D._Poyser" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:T. amp; A. D. Poyser"><a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>. amp; A. D. Poyser</a>, <small>→ISBN</small> |  republished as  <cite>The <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a>: Individuality in a Gregarious Wading Bird</cite> (Poyser Monographs), London |  <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>. amp; A. D. Poyser, 2010, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=9-yViWFSVS8Camp;pg=PA111">page 111</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">During late spring and early summer it becomes difficult to detect <b>Ruffs</b> in their breeding habitat. The males no longer visit the <a href = vnd.unilang:lek.html>leks</a>, and most have left the area. Some of the females may still be sitting on their eggs, invisible to casual passers-by.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">ornithology</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A set of lengthened or otherwise modified <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> on or around the neck of a bird.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1794</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Bartram" class="extiw" title="w:William Bartram">William Bartram</a>,  chapter V, in  <cite>Travels through North and South Carolina, Georgia, East and West Florida, the Cherokee Country, the Extensive Territories of the Muscogulges or Creek Confederacy, and the Country of the Chactaws. Containing an Account of the Soil and Natural Productions of those Regions; together with Observations on the Manners of the Indians. Embellished with Copper-plates</cite>, 2nd London edition, Philadelphia, <a href = vnd.unilang:pa.html>Pa</a>. |  Printed by James and Johnson; London: Reprinted for J. Johnson, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" class="extiw" title="w:St Paul | s Cathedral">St. Paul's Church-yard</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/941618708">941618708</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/travelsthroughno00bartpage/148/mode/1up/">pages 148–149</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">I ſhall call this bird the painted vulture. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> the head and neck bare of <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> nearly down to the ſtomach, when the <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> begin to cover the ſkin, and ſoon become long and of a ſoft texture, forming a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> or tippet, in which the bird by contracting his neck can hide that as well as his head: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2016</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Johnsgard" class="extiw" title="w:Paul Johnsgard">Paul A[ustin] Johnsgard</a>,  “Introduction to the North American Grouse”, in  <cite>The North American Grouse: Their Biology and Behavior</cite>, Lincoln, <a href = vnd.unilang:neb.html>Neb</a>. |  Zea Books, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=map5DAAAQBAJamp;pg=PA9">page 9</a>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">In the ruffed grouse, the special "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>" <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a> are borne on the lateral <a href = vnd.unilang:branches.html>branches</a> of the lower cervical feather tract.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">zoology</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A collar of lengthened or distinctively coloured fur on or around the neck of an animal.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2005</b>,  Eskandar Firouz,  “Mammals of Iran”, in  <cite>The Complete Fauna of Iran</cite>, London; New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I.B._Tauris" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:I.B. Tauris">I.B. Tauris</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=t2EZCScFXloCamp;pg=PA88">page 88</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The Afghan urial, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:smaller.html>smaller</a> than the Transcaspian urial, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> found in the mountains near Iran's eastern frontier, and <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the wild sheep of Afghanistan and western Pakistan. Its <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> black sprinkled with white hairs and its <a href = vnd.unilang:bib.html>bib</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> white.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2017</b> April,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_Brennan" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Marie Brennan"><a href = vnd.unilang:marie.html>Marie</a> Brennan</a> [pseudonym; Bryn Neuenschwander],  chapter 10, in  <cite>Within the Sanctuary of Wings: A Memoir by Lady <a href = vnd.unilang:trent.html>Trent</a></cite>, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tor_Books" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Tor Books">Tor Books</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=EzIaDAAAQBAJamp;pg=PA151">page 151</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The creature coming toward <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:went.html>went</a> instantly still. On the other side of the fire, one of them jerked upright and popped its <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> as wide as it would go. The other lunged to the side of the second and clamped one clawed hand around its muzzle.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">engineering</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A collar on a shaft or other piece to prevent endwise motion.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1835</b> January,  “A Method of Working the <a href = vnd.unilang:slides.html>Slides</a> and Valves of Steam Engines when Using Steam Expansively”, in  <cite>The Repertory of Patent Inventions, and Other Discoveries amp; Improvements in <a href = vnd.unilang:arts.html>Arts</a>, Manufactures, and Agriculture; <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span></cite>, volume III, number XIII (New Series), London |  Published for the proprietor, by Simpkin, Marshall, and Co. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Worshipful_Company_of_Stationers_and_Newspaper_Makers" class="extiw" title="w:Worshipful Company of Stationers and Newspaper Makers">Stationers' Hall Court</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/191047082">191047082</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=l70-AAAAcAAJamp;pg=PA63">page 63</a>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The stroke of the cut-off valves <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> very short, and the <b>ruffs</b> on the parts, <i>g</i>, <i>g</i>, regulate its length.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1846</b> February 25,  “Specification of the Patent Granted to William Robertson, Machine-maker, of Gateside, in the Parish of Neilston, Renfrewshire, for Certain Improvements in the Machinery for Spinning and Twisting Cotton, Silk, Wool, Flax, and Other Fibrous Substances.—Sealed Feb. 25, 1846”, in  <cite>The Repertory of Patent Inventions, and Other Discoveries amp; Improvements in <a href = vnd.unilang:arts.html>Arts</a>, Manufactures, and Agriculture; <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span></cite>, volume VIII, number 4 (Enlarged Series), London |  Published for the proprietor, by Alexander Macintosh, Great New Street; and <a href = vnd.unilang:sold.html>sold</a> by Simpkin, Marshall, and Co., Stationers' Hall Court; J. Weale, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Holborn" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:High Holborn">High Holborn</a>; and G. Hebert, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheapside" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Cheapside">Cheapside</a>, published October 1846, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/191047082">191047082</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=9so-AAAAcAAJamp;pg=PA205">page 205</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">This plate <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> a <a href = vnd.unilang:slot.html>slot</a> in it lengthwise to admit of its being shifted a sixth part of the circumference of the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> An exhibition of haughtiness or pride.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1694</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesop" class="extiw" title="w:Aesop">Aesop</a> |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_L%27Estrange" class="extiw" title="w:Roger L | Estrange"><a href = vnd.unilang:roger.html>Roger</a> L'Estrange</a>,  “Fab<span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>le<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span> XXXVIII. A Horse and an Ass.”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesop%27s_Fables" class="extiw" title="w:Aesop | s Fables">Fables, of Æsop and Other Eminent Mythologists: With Morals and Reflexions</a></cite>, 2nd corrected and amended edition, London |  Printed for <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>[ichard] Sare, B[enjamin] <a href = vnd.unilang:took.html>Took</a>, M[atthew] Gillyflower, A. amp; J. Churchil[l], J[oseph] Hindmarsh, and G[eorge] Sawbridge, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/606109080">606109080</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=PmeVqZaojKACamp;pg=RA1-PA39">page 39</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Nay, how many Emperours and <a href = vnd.unilang:princes.html>Princes</a>, that in the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a></b> of all their Glory have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:taken.html>taken</a> down from the Head of a Conquering Army, to the Wheel of the <a href = vnd.unilang:victor.html>Victor</a>'s Chariot?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Tumultuous or wanton conduct or procedure.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1549</b> March 15,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugh_Latimer" class="extiw" title="w:Hugh Latimer">Hugh <a href = vnd.unilang:latimer.html>Latimer</a></a>,  “The Second Sermon of Master Hugh <a href = vnd.unilang:latimer.html>Latimer</a>, which He Preached before the King’s Majesty, within His <a href = vnd.unilang:grace.html>Grace</a>’s Palace at Westminster, the Fifteenth Day of March, 1549”, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Corrie_(priest)" class="extiw" title="w:George Corrie (priest)">George Elwes Corrie</a>, editor, <cite>The Works of Hugh <a href = vnd.unilang:latimer.html>Latimer</a>, sometime Bishop of Worcester, Martyr, 1555. George Elwes Corrie, B.D. <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span></cite>, volume I, Cambridge |  Printed at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press" class="extiw" title="w:Cambridge University Press">University Press</a>, published 1844, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/796947594">796947594</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=NJkqAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA109">pages 108–109</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Thou must not pill and poll thy tenant, that thou mayest have, as they say, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:unde.html>Unde</a></i>, and that thy never enough, to ruffle it out in a riotous <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>, and a prodigal, dissolute, and licentious living.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To shape (fabric, etc.) into a <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a>; to adorn (a garment, etc.) with a <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1810</b> December 6,  H. <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>.,  “Venus Preserved; or, The Plot Discovered”, in  <cite>The Monthly Repertory of English Literature, <a href = vnd.unilang:arts.html>Arts</a>, Sciences, etc.</cite>, volume XII, number XLVIII, Paris |  Printed by Belin, rue <a href = vnd.unilang:des.html>des</a> Mathurins-St.-Jacques, Hôtel Cluny; for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Anthony_Galignani" class="extiw" title="w:John Anthony Galignani">Galignani</a>, (late Parsons, Galignani, and Co.) bookseller, rue Vivienne, No. 17, published March 1811, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/472474509">472474509</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Pi5ZAAAAcAAJamp;pg=PA490">page 490</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The <a href = vnd.unilang:ladies.html>ladies</a> have <a href = vnd.unilang:been.html>been</a> <i>carped at</i>, and their <i>dress</i>; / You <a href = vnd.unilang:wanted.html>wanted</a> them <i><b>ruffed</b> up</i> like good <span style="font-variant:small-caps;">Queen Bess</span>; <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> falconry</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Of a falcon, hawk, etc.: to hit (the prey) without fixing or grabbing hold of it.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1888</b>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Words" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Good Words">Good <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>Words</a></a></cite>, volume 29, London |  Alexander Strahan and Co., <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/1009003628">1009003628</a></small>, page 616:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Instantly the keen-eyed hawk "stooped," or descended, with a rushing swoop, and struck one of the <a href = vnd.unilang:birds.html>birds</a> with her claws, but without killing it, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> called "rifling," or "<b>ruffing</b>" it.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:rare.html>rare</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To ruffle; to disorder.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1590</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Spenser" class="extiw" title="w:Edmund Spenser">Edmund Spenser</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Faerie_Queene" class="extiw" title="w:The Faerie Queene">The Faerie Qveene.<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Disposed into Twelue Books, Fashioning XII. Morall Vertues">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, London |  Printed [by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wolfe_(printer)" class="extiw" title="w:John Wolfe (printer)">John Wolfe</a>] for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Ponsonby_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:William Ponsonby (publisher)">VVilliam Ponsonbie</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/960102938">960102938</a></small>, book III, canto II, stanza 27, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/faeriequeenedispo00spenpage/418/mode/1up">page 418</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Thenceforth the fether in her lofty creſt, / <b>Ruffed</b> of loue, <a href = vnd.unilang:gan.html>gan</a> lowly to auaile, / And her prowd portaunce, and her princely geſt, / VVith which ſhe earſt tryumphed, now <a href = vnd.unilang:did.html>did</a> quaile: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1818</b> December 15,  “To <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morris_Birkbeck" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Morris Birkbeck">Morris Birkbeck</a>, Esq. of English Prairie, Illinois Territory. <li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete<span class="ib-comma">,</span> transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Of a bird: to ruffle its <a href = vnd.unilang:feathers.html>feathers</a>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tor_Seidler" class="extiw" title="w:Tor Seidler">Tor Seidler</a>,  chapter 1, in  <cite>Firstborn</cite> (A Caitlyn Dloughy Book), New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheneum_Books" class="extiw" title="w:Atheneum Books"><a href = vnd.unilang:atheneum.html>Atheneum</a> Books for Young Readers</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Bf3QAwAAQBAJamp;pg=PA7">page 7</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">"Scat," the crow <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a>. <hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg/200px-Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg/300px-Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg/400px-Gymnocephalus_cernuus_Hungary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="317" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Eurasian <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> or ruffe (<span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gymnocephalus_cernua" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gymnocephalus cernua"><i>Gymnocephalus cernua</i></a></span> or <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gymnocephalus_cernuus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gymnocephalus cernuus"><i>Gymnocephalus cernuus</i></a></span>; <i>sense 1</i>)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG/200px-Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG" decoding="async" width="200" height="67" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG/300px-Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG/400px-Tommy_Ruff_1.PNG 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="900" /></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_herring" class="extiw" title="w:Australian herring">Australian herring</a> (<span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Arripis_georgianus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Arripis georgianus"><i>Arripis georgianus</i></a></span>; <i>sense 2</i>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>Possibly from <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">rough</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Alternative spelling of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">ruffe</i></span></span>: a small freshwater fish of the genus <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gymnocephalus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gymnocephalus"><i>Gymnocephalus</i></a></span>; <i>specifically</i> the Eurasian ruffe (<span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gymnocephalus_cernua" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gymnocephalus cernua"><i>Gymnocephalus cernua</i></a></span> or <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Gymnocephalus_cernuus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Gymnocephalus cernuus"><i>Gymnocephalus cernuus</i></a></span>) which <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> spiny <a href = vnd.unilang:fins.html>fins</a>; the <span class="Latn" lang="en">pope</span>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source">[<b>1661</b>,  Robert Lovell,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=U08PAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PA56-IA3">Isagoge Zoologicomineralogica. Or An Introduction to the History of Animals and Minerals, or <i>Panzoographie</i>, and <i>Pammineralogie</i></a>”, in  <cite><span class="Grek" lang="el">ΠΑΝΖΩΟΡΥΚΤΟΛΟΓΙΑ</span> <span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>Panzōoryktologia<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span>. Sive Panzoologicomineralogia. Or a Compleat History of Animals and Minerals, Containing the Summe of All Authors, both Ancient and Modern, Galenicall and Chymicall, <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span></cite>, Oxford |  Printed by <a href = vnd.unilang:hen.html>Hen</a>[<a href = vnd.unilang:ry.html>ry</a>] Hall, for <a href = vnd.unilang:jos.html>Jos</a>[eph] Godwin, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/79920846">79920846</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Of <i>Fiſhes</i> thoſe <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> feed on in England, are either <i>ſcaled</i>, as ſturgian, ſalmon, grailing, ſhuins, carps, breams, the barbel, <a href = vnd.unilang:mullet.html>mullet</a>, pike, <a href = vnd.unilang:luce.html>luce</a>, perch, <b>ruffs</b>, herrings, ſprats, pilchers, roche, ſhads, dorry, gudgin, and umbers;<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></span><dl><dl><dd><span class="e-footer"><small>It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not clear which species of fish <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> referred to in this work.</small></span>]</dd></dl></dl></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1703</b>,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=VHhUAAAAYAAJamp;pg=PP152"><em>Norfolk</em></a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/An_Universal,_Historical,_Geographical,_Chronological_and_Poetical_Dictionary" class="extiw" title="w:An Universal, Historical, Geographical, Chronological and Poetical Dictionary">An Universal, Historical, Geographical, Chronological and Poetical Dictionary, <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Exactly Describing the Situation, Extent, Customs, Laws, Manners, Commodities, amp;c. of All Kingdoms, Common-wealths, Provinces, Islands and Cities, in the Known World. Containing likewise the Lives of the Patriarchs, Prophets, Apostles, and Primitive Fathers; Emperors, Kings, Princes, Popes, Cardinals, Bishops, and Other Eminent Persons; with an Account of the Inventors and Improvers of Arts and Sciences, Philosophers, and All Celebrated Authors. Also the History of the Pagan Gods, Very Useful for the Understanding of Classick Authors; of the Several Sects among the Jews, Christians, Heathens and Mahometans, with Their Principal Ceremonies, Games and Festivals; of General Councils and Synods, when, and where Assembled; of the Establishment and Progress of Religious and Military Orders; and of the Genealogies of the Most Illustrious Families, especially our English, Scotch and Irish. The Whole Consisting of a Curious Miscellany of Sacred and Prophane History, Extracted from Moreri, Bayle, Baudrand, Hoffman, Danet, and Many More of the Best and Choicest Historians, Geographers, Chronologers and Lexicographers, Antient and Modern.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> In Two <a href = vnd.unilang:volumes.html>Volumes</a></a></cite>, volume II, London |  Printed for J. <a href = vnd.unilang:hartley.html>Hartley</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="next the Kings-Head Tavern in Holborn">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>; W. Turner,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="at the Angel in Lincolns-Inn Back Gate">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>; and Tho[<a href = vnd.unilang:mas.html>mas</a>] Hodgson,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="over against Grays-Inn Gate in Holborn.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/642289644">642289644</a></small>, column 2:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Its Principal <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>[iver] of all thoſe mention'd, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the <i>Yare</i> on which <i>Norwich</i> and <i>Yarmouth</i> ſtands, in which <a href = vnd.unilang:r.html>R</a>[iver] the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a></b>, a Fish <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> found, remarkable for being all <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:prickles.html>Prickles</a>; [...]</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li class="senseid" id="English-Arripis_georgianus"><span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Arripis_georgianus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Arripis georgianus"><i>Arripis georgianus</i></a></span>, a fish found in <a href = vnd.unilang:cool.html>cool</a> waters off the southern coast of Australia; the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_herring" class="extiw" title="w:Australian herring">Australian herring</a> or <a href = vnd.unilang:tommy.html>tommy</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2014</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Davidson_(food_writer)" class="extiw" title="w:Alan Davidson (food writer)">Alan Davidson</a>,  “Australasian ‘salmon’”, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Jaine" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Tom Jaine"><a href = vnd.unilang:tom.html>Tom</a> Jaine</a>, editor, <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Oxford_Companion_to_Food" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Oxford Companion to Food">The Oxford Companion to Food</a></cite>, 3rd edition, Oxford |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=RL6LAwAAQBAJamp;pg=PA44">page 44</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">In the same genus there <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> another species which <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> better eating. This <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <i>A</i>[<i>rripis</i>] <i>georgianus</i>, popularly known as the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> or <a href = vnd.unilang:tommy.html>tommy</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> (again, nothing to do with anything bearing that name in the Old World), but now officially called 'Australian herring' (another aberration). [...] The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>, on the other hand, although a <a href = vnd.unilang:smaller.html>smaller</a> fish, <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> good eating; its flesh <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> tender and tasty.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A bottom-dwelling carnivorous fish of the family Sparidae found in temperate and tropical waters; a porgy or sea bream.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source">[<b>1677</b>,  Thomas Holyoke [<i>i.e.</i>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Holyoake" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Thomas Holyoake">Thomas Holyoake</a>],  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=cjdLAAAAcAAJamp;pg=PT107">A <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a>, or Sea-bream</a>”, in  <cite>A Large Dictionary in Three Parts: I. The English before the Latin, Containing above Ten Thousand <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>Words</a> More Than any Dictionary yet Extant. II. The Proper Names of Persons, <a href = vnd.unilang:places.html>Places</a>, and Other <a href = vnd.unilang:things.html>Things</a> Necessary to the Understanding of Historians and <a href = vnd.unilang:poets.html>Poets</a>. <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span></cite>, London |  Printed by W[illiam] Rawlins, for G[eorge] Sawbridge, W[illiam] Place, <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>[homas] <a href = vnd.unilang:basset.html>Basset</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Dring" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Dring"><a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>[homas] <a href = vnd.unilang:dring.html>Dring</a></a>, J[ohn] Leigh and J[ohn] Place, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/863465780">863465780</a></small>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><i>A <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a></b>, or Sea-bream.</i> Melanurus.</span>]</div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">Australian herring (<i>Arripis georgianus</i>)</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">roughy</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">roffle</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">rouffle</i> (earlier <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">romfle</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">ronfle</i>), or from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">ronfa</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">card game similar to <a href = vnd.unilang:whist.html>whist</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>; these <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>words</a> are possibly from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">triomphe</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">a triumph, victory</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">trionfo</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">triumph; trump card</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup> from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">triumphus</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">hymn to Bacchus; celebration, triumph</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">θρῐ́ᾰμβος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">thríambos</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">hymn to Dionysius, thriambus</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. The verb <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> derived from the noun.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_2">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffed</b>) <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">card games</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive, intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To play a trump card to a trick when unable to follow suit (that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a>, to play a card of the same suit as the previous or leading card). <span class="defdate">[late 16th c.]</span>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2005</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Horton_(bridge)" class="extiw" title="w:Mark Horton (bridge)">Mark Horton</a>,  “2004: <a href = vnd.unilang:loser.html>Loser</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:takes.html>Takes</a> Nothing”, in <a href = vnd.unilang:ray.html>Ray</a> Lee, editor, <cite>The Hands of Time: The <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>Best</a> 100 Bridge <a href = vnd.unilang:deals.html>Deals</a> Ever Played!</cite>, Toronto, <a href = vnd.unilang:ont.html>Ont</a>. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_Point_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Master Point Press">Master Point Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=NIA9u1GGy2ICamp;pg=PA181">page 181</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zia_Mahmood" class="extiw" title="w:Zia Mahmood"><a href = vnd.unilang:zia.html>Zia</a> [Mahmood]</a> <b>ruffed</b> the club return and then played the ace of <a href = vnd.unilang:hearts.html>hearts</a> and a heart, leaving declarer with another spade <a href = vnd.unilang:loser.html>loser</a> for two down.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2014</b>,  D. K. Acharya,  <cite>Standard Methods of Contract Bridge Complete: A Methodical Study and Critical Analysis of Bidding, Play, Defence and Other Strategic Instruments including Illustration of about 200 <a href = vnd.unilang:deals.html>Deals</a></cite>, India |  Partridge, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penguin_Random_House" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Penguin Random House">Penguin Random House</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=a0gTBQAAQBAJamp;pg=PA181">page 181</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The declarer may not have fear of losing control on trumps, because <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> after <b>ruffing</b> in one hand, the other hand will have sufficient length to draw the trumps. A 4-4 fit of trumps <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> considered to be the <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>best</a> and most convenient for the declarer. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> He can easily make 5 or 6 or <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> 7 tricks in trumps by way of <b>ruffing</b> once, twice or thrice in one hand.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <i>Especially in the form</i> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> out</b>: to defeat (a card, etc.) by ruffing, thus establishing the master card in the suit <a href = vnd.unilang:led.html>led</a>.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1999</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zia_Mahmood" class="extiw" title="w:Zia Mahmood"><a href = vnd.unilang:zia.html>Zia</a> Mahmood</a> |  David Burn,  “The Shriek”, in <a href = vnd.unilang:ray.html>Ray</a> Lee, editor, <cite>Around the World in 80 Hands</cite>, Toronto, <a href = vnd.unilang:ont.html>Ont</a>. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_Point_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Master Point Press">Master Point Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=3X22r6Y2d3YCamp;pg=PA15">page 15</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Then I played on <a href = vnd.unilang:diamonds.html>diamonds</a>, to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> out the suit – but East <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> four <a href = vnd.unilang:diamonds.html>diamonds</a> and West none, so I <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> annoyingly to lose a trick to East's ♣K in the end.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2016</b>,  <a href = vnd.unilang:ken.html>Ken</a> Casey,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=USwyDAAAQBAJamp;pg=PP11">Introduction: Focus Your Attention on Ruffing <a href = vnd.unilang:losers.html>Losers</a></a>”, in  <cite>Playing Beginning Bridge</cite>, [Bloomington, Ind.] |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xlibris" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Xlibris">Xlibris</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">It never ceases to amaze <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> how many times people get in trouble by failing to first <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> out their sure <a href = vnd.unilang:losers.html>losers</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms_2">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">trump</span></li></ul>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_3">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>) <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">card games</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span>
</p>
<ol><li>An instance of ruffing, or an opportunity to <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a>, when unable to follow suit. <span class="defdate">[late 16th c.]</span>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2008</b>,  Phillip Alder,  “The Just-So Story of a Justified Ruff-and-Sluff”, in  <cite>The New York Times</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2008/01/19/crosswords/bridge/19CARD.html">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Take, for example, the axiom "Never give declarer a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>-and-sluff."</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A game similar to <a href = vnd.unilang:whist.html>whist</a> and its predecessor. <span class="defdate">[late 16th c.]</span>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1595</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Peele" class="extiw" title="w:George Peele">G[eorge] P[eele]</a>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Old_Wives%27_Tale_(play)" class="extiw" title="w:The Old Wives |  Tale (play)">The Old Wiues Tale. A Pleasant Conceited Comedie, Played by the Queenes Maiesties Players</a></cite>, London |  Printed at London by Iohn Danter, and are to be <a href = vnd.unilang:sold.html>sold</a> by Raph Hancocke, and Iohn Hardie, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/222301598">222301598</a></small> |  reprinted as  | <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._W._Greg" class="extiw" title="w:W. W. Greg"><a href = vnd.unilang:walter.html>Walter</a> Wilson Greg</a> | , editor, <cite>The Old <a href = vnd.unilang:wives.html>Wives</a>’ Tale: 1595</cite> (The Malone Society Reprints |  7), [Oxford] |  Printed for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malone_Society" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Malone Society">Malone Society</a> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horace_Hart" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Horace Hart">Horace <a href = vnd.unilang:hart.html>Hart</a></a> M.A. at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>, 1908, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/614540367">614540367</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/oldwivestale00peeluoftpage/n29/mode/1up/">85–87</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[W]hat ſhall <a href = vnd.unilang:wee.html>wee</a> haue a game at Trumpe or <b>Ruffe</b> to driue away the time, how ſay you?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Onomatopoeic.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">music<span class="ib-comma">,</span> often military</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A low, vibrating beat of a drum, quieter than a roll; a ruffle.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2003</b>,  Rob <a href = vnd.unilang:lewis.html>Lewis</a>,  “3 Camps: Rudimental Drum Solo”, in  <cite>Crosstraining: A Method for Applying Rhythms and Techniques to Drum Set, Hand Percussion and Mallet Instruments</cite>, Pacific, Mo. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mel_Bay" class="extiw" title="w:Mel Bay"><a href = vnd.unilang:mel.html>Mel</a> Bay Productions</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, part 6 (Rudiments and Rudimental Solos), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=LrOTvH2rnvECamp;pg=PA71">page 71</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">I also used quite a few of the flat-fingered <a href = vnd.unilang:kind.html>kind</a> of <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b> (as used before on the doumbek in the baladi section) to embellish some notes.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb_3">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">ruffs</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">ruffed</b>) <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">music<span class="ib-comma">,</span> often military</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To beat a <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> or ruffle, as on a drum.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1823</b> February,  Nalla,  “Corporal Colville”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_London_Magazine" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The London Magazine">The London Magazine</a></cite>, volume VII, London |  Printed for <a href = vnd.unilang:taylor.html>Taylor</a> and Hessey, 93, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fleet_Street" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Fleet Street">Fleet Street</a>, and 13, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterloo,_London" class="extiw" title="w:Waterloo, London">Waterloo Place</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/977280548">977280548</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gtcYAAAAMAAJamp;pg=PA136">page 136</a>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[A] wooden <a href = vnd.unilang:leg.html>leg</a> and an empty coat sleeve, and fourteen poor <a href = vnd.unilang:pennies.html>pennies</a> a-day, are all that I have got by allowing myself to be seduced by the cursed din of a Scotchman's bagpipe. I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> once a good yeoman, in <a href = vnd.unilang:kent.html>Kent</a>, and in an evil hour <a href = vnd.unilang:went.html>went</a> to the fair at Maidstone. The drum <b>ruffed</b>, and the pipe screamed in the market-place, and away I <a href = vnd.unilang:went.html>went</a> to see what <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> to happen. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> I fairly <a href = vnd.unilang:forgot.html>forgot</a> myself, and scarcely ever <a href = vnd.unilang:knew.html>knew</a> where I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> or what I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> doing, till I found myself on board a ship, and saw the olive hills and vineyards of Spain, <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Of a drum, etc.: to have a <a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a> or ruffle beaten on it.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1836</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyrone_Power_(Irish_actor)" class="extiw" title="w:Tyrone Power (Irish actor)"><a href = vnd.unilang:tyrone.html>Tyrone</a> Power</a>,  “Trenton Falls”, in  <cite>Impressions of America, during the Years 1833, 1834, and 1835. <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span> In Two <a href = vnd.unilang:volumes.html>Volumes</a></cite>, volume I, London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bentley_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Richard Bentley (publisher)">Richard Bentley</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Burlington_Street" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:New Burlington Street">New Burlington Street</a>, publisher in ordinary to His Majesty, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/1003943032">1003943032</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=rsJBAQAAMAAJamp;pg=PA384">page 384</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">If anything could have kept <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> awake, this cracked drum would; and, in truth, I <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> my fears, when, on entering my room, I <a href = vnd.unilang:heard.html>heard</a> my hero <b>ruffing</b> it away immediately in front of the window; but they <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> groundless apprehensions, though his efforts <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> varied and unceasing, for I undressed to the tune of the "<a href = vnd.unilang:grenadiers.html>Grenadiers</a>' March," stepped into <a href = vnd.unilang:bed.html>bed</a> to the "<a href = vnd.unilang:reveille.html>Reveille</a>," and dropped fast asleep to the first part of "Yankee <a href = vnd.unilang:doodle.html>Doodle</a>!"</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>The bark of a dog; arf, woof.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2014</b>,  <a href = vnd.unilang:suzan.html>Suzan</a> Kayaalp,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pzoaBwAAQBAJamp;pg=PT27">The Visitor</a>”, in  <cite>The Adventures of Lucky the Duck</cite>, New York, N.Y. |  Page Publishing, <small>→ISBN</small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">"<b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>Ruff</a></b>, <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ruff.html>ruff</a></b>!" Around the corner, a little light brown, short-haired dog <a href = vnd.unilang:came.html>came</a> running. On seeing the little brown terrier, Annie and <a href = vnd.unilang:marie.html>Marie</a> looked at one another. Letting out a moan, Annie <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a>, "<a href = vnd.unilang:oh.html>Oh</a> no, it's JB! I wish Joyce would take him to dog school and have him taught some manners."</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">colloquial</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Alternative spelling of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">rough</i></span></span>.

***ruggenprik.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:ruggenprik.html>ruggenprik</a> (63171)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Compound of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:rug.html>rug</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">back</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">-en-</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:prik.html>prik</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">jab, shot</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruggenprik.html>ruggenprik</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruggenprikken.html>ruggenprikken</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ruggenprik.html>ruggenprikje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>An injection of a substance for spinal anaesthesia.</li></ol>
